[ctrl-option-j]" accesskey="j"><span>What links here</span></a></li><li id="t-recentchangeslinked" class="mw-list-item"><a href="/wiki/Special:RecentChangesLinked/Key_events_of_the_20th_century" 	</div>
</div>

				<div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body ve-init-mw-desktopArticleTarget-targetContainer" aria-labelledby="firstHeading" data-mw-ve-target-container="">
					<div class="vector-body-before-content">
							<div class="mw-indicators">
		</div>

						<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
					</div>
					<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-content-subtitle"></div></div>
					
					
					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/20th_century" title="20th century">20th century</a> changed the world in unprecedented ways. The <a href="/wiki/World_Wars" class="mw-redirect" title="World Wars">World Wars</a> sparked tension between countries and led to the creation of <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Atomic bomb">atomic bombs</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> led to the <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">Space Race</a> and the creation of space-based rockets, and the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a> was created. These advancements have played a significant role in citizens' lives and shaped the <a href="/wiki/21st_century" title="21st century">21st century</a> into what it is today.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc">
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Historic_events_in_the_20th_century">Historic events in the 20th century</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Historic events in the 20th century"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="World_at_the_beginning_of_the_century">World at the beginning of the century</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: World at the beginning of the century"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Edwardian_era" title="Edwardian era">Edwardian era</a></div>
<p>The new beginning of the 20th century marked significant changes. The 1900s saw the decade herald a series of inventions, including the <a href="/wiki/Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile">automobile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airplane" title="Airplane">airplane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Radio_broadcasting" title="Radio broadcasting">radio broadcasting</a>.
</p><p>From 1914 to 1918, the First World War, and its aftermath, caused major changes in the power balance of the world, destroying or transforming some of the most powerful empires.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="&quot;The_war_to_end_all_wars&quot;:_World_War_I_(19141918)"><span id=".22The_war_to_end_all_wars.22:_World_War_I_.281914.E2.80.931918.29"></span>"The war to end all wars": World War I (19141918)</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: &quot;The war to end all wars&quot;: World War I (19141918)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Gavrilo_Princip_captured_in_Sarajevo_1914.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Gavrilo_Princip_captured_in_Sarajevo_1914.jpg/220px-Gavrilo_Princip_captured_in_Sarajevo_1914.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Gavrilo_Princip_captured_in_Sarajevo_1914.jpg/330px-Gavrilo_Princip_captured_in_Sarajevo_1914.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Gavrilo_Princip_captured_in_Sarajevo_1914.jpg/440px-Gavrilo_Princip_captured_in_Sarajevo_1914.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1602" data-file-height="1028"></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Arrest_of_a_suspect_in_Sarajevo" class="mw-redirect" title="Arrest of a suspect in Sarajevo">Arrest of a suspect in Sarajevo</a> following the <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_Archduke_Franz_Ferdinand" title="Assassination of Archduke Franz Ferdinand">Assassination of Archduke Franz Ferdinand</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>The First World War (or simply WWI), termed "The Great War" by contemporaries, started in 1914 and ended in 1918. The war and by extension the century as a whole was <a href="/wiki/Plot_(narrative)" title="Plot (narrative)">ignited</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_Archduke_Franz_Ferdinand_of_Austria" class="mw-redirect" title="Assassination of Archduke Franz Ferdinand of Austria">Assassination in Sarajevo</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Hungarian Empire">Austro-Hungarian Empire</a>'s heir to the throne, Erzherzog <a href="/wiki/Archduke_Franz_Ferdinand_of_Austria" title="Archduke Franz Ferdinand of Austria">Franz Ferdinand</a>, by <a href="/wiki/Gavrilo_Princip" title="Gavrilo Princip">Gavrilo Princip</a> of the organization "<a href="/wiki/Young_Bosnia" title="Young Bosnia">Young Bosnia</a>," Bosnian Serbs' liberation movement. This was similar to how the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">9/11</a> was the inciting incident of the <a href="/wiki/21st_century" title="21st century">21st century</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Bound by Slavic nationalism to help the small Serbian state, the Russians came to the aid of the Serbs when they were attacked. Interwoven alliances, an increasing arms race, and old hatreds dragged Europe into the war.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Allies, known initially as "The <a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">Triple Entente</a>", comprised the British Empire, France, and Russia. Germany, <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, and later the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, were known as "The <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 1917, Russia ended hostile actions against the Central Powers after the fall of the Tsar. The Bolsheviks negotiated the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk" title="Treaty of Brest-Litovsk">Treaty of Brest-Litovsk</a> with Germany, although it was a huge cost to Russia. In the treaty, Bolshevik Russia ceded the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a> to Germany, and its province of <a href="/wiki/Kars_Oblast" class="mw-redirect" title="Kars Oblast">Kars Oblast</a> in the <a href="/wiki/South_Caucasus" title="South Caucasus">South Caucasus</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. It also recognized the independence of <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_People%27s_Republic" title="Ukrainian People's Republic">Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Although Germany shifted huge forces from the eastern to the western front after signing the treaty, it was unable to stop the Allied advance, especially with the entrance of American troops in 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The war itself was also a chance for the combatant nations to show off their military strength and technological ingenuity. The Germans introduced the machine gun,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/U-boats" class="mw-redirect" title="U-boats">U-boats</a><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and deadly gases.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The British first used the <a href="/wiki/Tank" title="Tank">tank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Both sides had a chance to test out their new aircraft to see if they could be used in warfare. It was widely believed that the war would be short. Unfortunately, since <a href="/wiki/Trench_warfare" title="Trench warfare">trench warfare</a> was the best form of defense, advances on both sides were very slow and came at a terrible cost to lives.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Dissolution_of_Austria-Hungary.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Dissolution_of_Austria-Hungary.png/220px-Dissolution_of_Austria-Hungary.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="130" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Dissolution_of_Austria-Hungary.png/330px-Dissolution_of_Austria-Hungary.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Dissolution_of_Austria-Hungary.png/440px-Dissolution_of_Austria-Hungary.png 2x" data-file-width="1641" data-file-height="970"></a><figcaption>Division of <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> after World War I</figcaption></figure>
<p>When the war was finally over in 1918, the results would set the stage for the next twenty years. First and foremost, the Germans were forced to sign the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>, forcing them to make exorbitant payments to repair damages caused during the War. Many Germans felt these reparations were unfair because they did not actually "lose" the war nor did they feel they caused the war (see <a href="/wiki/Stab-in-the-back_legend" class="mw-redirect" title="Stab-in-the-back legend">Stab-in-the-back legend</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Germany was never occupied by Allied troops, yet it had to accept a liberal democratic government imposed on it by the victors after the abdication of <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_II,_German_Emperor" class="mw-redirect" title="Wilhelm II, German Emperor">Kaiser Wilhelm</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Much of the map of Europe was redrawn by the victors based upon the theory that future wars could be prevented if all ethnic groups had their own "homeland".  New states like <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> were created out of the former Austro-Hungarian Empire to accommodate the nationalist aspirations of these groups.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>  An international body called the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> was formed to mediate disputes and prevent future wars, although its effectiveness was severely limited by, among other things, its reluctance and inability to act.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Russian_Revolution_and_communism">Russian Revolution and communism</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Russian Revolution and communism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a></div>
<p>The Russian Revolution of 1917 (ending in the overthrow of the Tsarist regime and the execution of His Imperial Majesty <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_II" title="Nicholas II">Nicholas II</a> and his family) sparked a wave of <a href="/wiki/Communist_revolution" title="Communist revolution">communist revolutions</a> across Europe, prompting many to believe that a socialist <a href="/wiki/World_revolution" title="World revolution">world revolution</a> could be realized in the near future.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> However, the European revolutions were defeated, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> died in 1924, and within a few years, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a> displaced <a href="/wiki/Leon_Trotsky" title="Leon Trotsky">Leon Trotsky</a> as the <i>de facto</i> leader of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. The idea of worldwide revolution was no longer in the forefront, as Stalin concentrated on "<a href="/wiki/Socialism_in_one_country" title="Socialism in one country">socialism in one country</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and embarked on a bold plan of collectivization and industrialization.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The majority of socialists and even many communists became disillusioned with Stalin's autocratic rule, his purges and the assassination of his "enemies", as well as the news of <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famines</a> he imposed on his own people.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Communism was strengthened as a force in Western democracies when the global economy crashed in 1929 in what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>. Many people saw this as the first stage of the end of the capitalist system and were attracted to Communism as a solution to the economic crisis, especially as the Soviet Union's economic development in the 1930s was strong, unaffected by the capitalist world's crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Between_the_wars">Between the wars</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Between the wars"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lange-MigrantMother02.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Lange-MigrantMother02.jpg/220px-Lange-MigrantMother02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="286" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Lange-MigrantMother02.jpg/330px-Lange-MigrantMother02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Lange-MigrantMother02.jpg/440px-Lange-MigrantMother02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6205" data-file-height="8066"></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Dorothea_Lange" title="Dorothea Lange">Dorothea Lange</a>'s 1936 photo <i>Migrant Mother</i> is one of the most iconic photos associated with the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a></figcaption></figure>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">Interwar period</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Economic_depression">Economic depression</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Economic depression"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Roaring_Twenties" title="Roaring Twenties">Roaring Twenties</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a></div> 
<p>After World War I, the global economy <a href="/wiki/Roaring_Twenties" title="Roaring Twenties">remained strong</a> through most of the 1920s. The war had provided a stimulus for industry and economic activity in general. There were many warning signs foretelling the <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Crash_of_1929" title="Wall Street Crash of 1929">Crash of 29</a> of the global <a href="/wiki/Economic_system" title="Economic system">economic system</a> at the end of the decade, that were generally not understood by the political leadership of the time.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The responses to the crisis often made the situation worse, as millions of people watched their savings become next to worthless, and the idea of a steady job with a reasonable income fading away.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Many sought answers from alternative ideologies such as communism and fascism.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> They believed that the capitalist economic system was collapsing and that new ideas were required to meet the crisis. The early responses to the crisis were based on the assumption that the free market would correct itself. This, however, did very little to correct the crisis or to alleviate the suffering of many ordinary people. Thus, the idea that the existing system could be reformed by government intervention in the economy, rather than by continuing the <i><a href="/wiki/Laissez-faire" title="Laissez-faire">laissez-faire</a></i> approach, became prominent as a solution to the crisis. Democratic governments assumed the responsibility to provide needed services in society, and to alleviate poverty. Thus was born the <a href="/wiki/Welfare_state" title="Welfare state">welfare state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> These two politico-economic principles, the belief in government intervention and the welfare state, as opposed to the belief in the free market and private institutions, would define many political battles for the rest of the century.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="The_rise_of_dictatorship">The rise of dictatorship</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The rise of dictatorship"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">Fascism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Totalitarianism" title="Totalitarianism">Totalitarianism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship" title="Dictatorship">Dictatorship</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-14468,_Berlin,_NS-Boykott_gegen_j%C3%BCdische_Gesch%C3%A4fte_crop.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-14468%2C_Berlin%2C_NS-Boykott_gegen_j%C3%BCdische_Gesch%C3%A4fte_crop.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-14468%2C_Berlin%2C_NS-Boykott_gegen_j%C3%BCdische_Gesch%C3%A4fte_crop.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="195" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-14468%2C_Berlin%2C_NS-Boykott_gegen_j%C3%BCdische_Gesch%C3%A4fte_crop.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-14468%2C_Berlin%2C_NS-Boykott_gegen_j%C3%BCdische_Gesch%C3%A4fte_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-14468%2C_Berlin%2C_NS-Boykott_gegen_j%C3%BCdische_Gesch%C3%A4fte_crop.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-14468%2C_Berlin%2C_NS-Boykott_gegen_j%C3%BCdische_Gesch%C3%A4fte_crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="553" data-file-height="490"></a><figcaption>Nazi soldiers hang a poster on the window of Jewish-owned business, that says: "Germans, defend yourselves. Do not buy from Jews". Germany, 1933</figcaption></figure>
<p>Fascism first appeared in Italy with the rise to power of <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a> in 1922.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The ideology was supported by a large proportion of the upper classes as a strong challenge to the threat of communism.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>When <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> came to power in Germany in 1933, a new variant of fascism called <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazism</a> took over Germany and ended the German experiment with democracy. The <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a> in Germany was dedicated to the restoration of German honor and prestige, the unification of German-speaking peoples, and the annexation of Central and Eastern Europe as vassal states, with the <a href="/wiki/Slavic_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic peoples">Slavic</a> population to act as slave labor to serve German economic interests.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>  There was also a strong appeal to a mythical racial purity (the idea that Germans were the <i>Herrenvolk</i> or the "master race"), and a vicious <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">antisemitism</a> which promoted the idea of Jews as subhuman (<i>Untermensch</i>) and worthy only of extermination.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Many people in Western Europe and the United States greeted the rise of Hitler with relief or indifference.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> They could see nothing wrong with a strong Germany ready to take on the communist menace to the east. Antisemitism during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> was widespread as many were content to blame the Jews for causing the economic downturn.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Hitler began to put his plan in motion, annexing Austria in the <i><a href="/wiki/Anschluss" title="Anschluss">Anschluss</a></i>, or reunification of Austria to Germany, in 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> He then negotiated the annexation of the <a href="/wiki/Sudetenland" title="Sudetenland">Sudetenland</a>, a German-speaking mountainous area of <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Munich_Conference" class="mw-redirect" title="Munich Conference">Munich Conference</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The British were eager to avoid war and believed Hitler's assurance to protect the security of the Czech state.  Hitler annexed the rest of the Czech state shortly afterwards, indicating that he had ulterior motives.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Fascism was not the only form of dictatorship to rise in the post-war period.  Almost all of the new democracies in the nations of Eastern Europe collapsed and were replaced by <a href="/wiki/Authoritarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Authoritarian">authoritarian</a> regimes.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Spain also became a dictatorship under the leadership of General <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Totalitarian states attempted to achieve total control over their subjects as well as their total loyalty. They held the state above the individual, and were often responsible for some of the worst acts in history, such as the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a> Adolf Hitler perpetrated on <a href="/wiki/European_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="European Jews">European Jews</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/Great_Purge" title="Great Purge">Great Purge</a> Stalin perpetrated in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> in the 1930s.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Global_war:_World_War_II_(19391945)"><span id="Global_war:_World_War_II_.281939.E2.80.931945.29"></span>Global war: World War II (19391945)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Global war: World War II (19391945)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="The_war_in_Europe">The war in Europe</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: The war in Europe"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_Theater_of_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="European Theater of World War II">European Theater of World War II</a></div>
<p><i>This section provides a conversational overview of World War II in Europe. See main article for a fuller discussion.</i>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:MolotovRibbentropStalin.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/MolotovRibbentropStalin.jpg/220px-MolotovRibbentropStalin.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="270" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/MolotovRibbentropStalin.jpg/330px-MolotovRibbentropStalin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/MolotovRibbentropStalin.jpg/440px-MolotovRibbentropStalin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2386" data-file-height="2932"></a><figcaption>The signing of the <a href="/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact" title="MolotovRibbentrop Pact">MolotovRibbentrop Pact</a> in Moscow, 23 August 1939</figcaption></figure>
<p>Soon after the events in Czechoslovakia, Britain and France issued assurances of protection to Poland, which seemed to be next on Hitler's list. World War II officially began on 1 September 1939, when Hitler unleashed his <a href="/wiki/Blitzkrieg" title="Blitzkrieg">Blitzkrieg</a>, or lightning war, against Poland. Britain and France, much to Hitler's surprise, immediately declared war upon Germany, but the help they delivered to Poland was negligible.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Sixteen days later, Poland was attacked from the East by Soviet Union, acting in a secret alliance with Nazi Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> After only a few weeks, the Polish forces were overwhelmed, and its government fled to exile in London (see <a href="/wiki/Polish_government_in_Exile" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish government in Exile">Polish government in Exile</a>).
</p><p>In starting World War II, the Germans had unleashed a new type of warfare, characterized by highly mobile forces and the use of massed aircraft. The German strategy concentrated upon the devotion of the <i><a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a></i>, or German army, to the use of tank groups, called <a href="/wiki/Panzer" class="mw-redirect" title="Panzer">panzer</a> divisions, and groups of mobile infantry, in concert with relentless attacks from the air. Encirclement was also a major part of the strategy. This change smashed any expectations that the Second World War would be fought in the trenches like the first.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>As Hitler's forces conquered Poland, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, under General Secretary <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>, was acting out guarantees of territory under a secret part of a <a href="/wiki/Nonaggression_pact" class="mw-redirect" title="Nonaggression pact">nonaggression pact</a> between the USSR and Germany known as the <a href="/wiki/Nazi-Soviet_Pact" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi-Soviet Pact">MolotovRibbentrop Pact</a>. This treaty gave Stalin free rein to take the Baltic republics of <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, Latvia, and <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, as well as Eastern Poland, all of which would remain in Soviet possession after the war.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Stalin also launched an attack on Finland, which he hoped to reduce to little more than a Soviet puppet state, but the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> met staunch Finnish resistance in what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Winter_War" title="Winter War">Winter War</a> and succeeded in gaining only limited territory from the Finns.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> This action would later cause the Finns to ally with Germany when its attack on the Soviet Union came in 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Blitzkrieg">Blitzkrieg</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Blitzkrieg"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>After the defeat of Poland, a period known as the <a href="/wiki/Phony_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Phony War">Phony War</a> ensued during the winter of 19391940, which saw only limited military land operation on the <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Western Front (World War II)">Western Front</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> All of this changed on 10 May 1940, when the Germans launched a massive attack on the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a> (Belgium, the Netherlands, and <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>), most probably to surmount the <a href="/wiki/Maginot_Line" title="Maginot Line">Maginot Line</a> of defenses on the Franco-German border.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> This witnessed the incredible fall of <a href="/wiki/Eben_Emael" class="mw-redirect" title="Eben Emael">Eben Emael</a>, a Belgian fort considered impregnable and guarded by 600 Belgians, to a force of only 88 German <a href="/wiki/Paratrooper" title="Paratrooper">paratroopers</a>. The worst of this was that King <a href="/wiki/Leopold_III_of_Belgium" title="Leopold III of Belgium">Leopold III of Belgium</a> surrendered to the Germans on 28 May without warning his allies, exposing the entire flank of the Allied forces to German panzer groups.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Following the conquest of the Low Countries, Hitler occupied Denmark and Norway, beginning on 9 April 1940. Norway was strategically important because of its sea routes which supplied crucial Swedish <a href="/wiki/Ore" title="Ore">ore</a> to the Nazi war machine. Norway held on for a few crucial weeks, but Denmark surrendered after <a href="/wiki/German_invasion_of_Denmark_(1940)" title="German invasion of Denmark (1940)">only six hours</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Sweden was the only Scandinavian country to successfully maintain its neutrality throughout the war, with occasional breaches of neutrality in favor of both <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Germany</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Western Allies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>With the disaster in the Low Countries, France, considered at the time to have had the finest army in the world, lasted only four weeks, with Paris being occupied on 14 June. Three days later, Marshal <a href="/wiki/Philippe_P%C3%A9tain" title="Philippe Ptain">Philippe Ptain</a> surrendered to the Germans.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The debacle in France also led to one of the war's greatest mysteries, and Hitler's first great blunder, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dunkirk" title="Battle of Dunkirk">Dunkirk</a>, where a third of a million trapped British and French soldiers were evacuated by not only British war boats, but every craft the army could find, including fishing boats. Hitler refused to "risk" his panzers on an action at Dunkirk, listening to the advice of Air Minister <a href="/wiki/Hermann_G%C3%B6ring" title="Hermann Gring">Hermann Gring</a> and allowing the <i><a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a></i>, or German Air Force, to handle the job.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The irony of this was that the escaped men would form the core of the army that was to invade the beaches of <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a> in 1944. Hitler did not occupy all of France, but about three-quarters, including all of the Atlantic coast, allowing Marshal Ptain to remain as dictator of an area known as <a href="/wiki/Vichy_France" title="Vichy France">Vichy France</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> However, members of the escaped French Army formed around General <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> to create the <a href="/wiki/Free_French" class="mw-redirect" title="Free French">Free French</a> forces, which would continue to battle Hitler in the stead of an independent France.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> At this moment, Italy, under <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a>, declared war on the Allies on 10 June, thinking that the war was almost over, but he managed only to occupy a few hundred yards of French territory.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Throughout the war, the Italians would be more of a burden to the Nazis than a boon, and would later cost them precious time in Greece.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Heinkel_He_111_during_the_Battle_of_Britain.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Heinkel_He_111_during_the_Battle_of_Britain.jpg/220px-Heinkel_He_111_during_the_Battle_of_Britain.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="186" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Heinkel_He_111_during_the_Battle_of_Britain.jpg/330px-Heinkel_He_111_during_the_Battle_of_Britain.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Heinkel_He_111_during_the_Battle_of_Britain.jpg/440px-Heinkel_He_111_during_the_Battle_of_Britain.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="676"></a><figcaption>German <a href="/wiki/Heinkel_He_111" title="Heinkel He 111">Heinkel He 111</a> bombers during the Battle of Britain</figcaption></figure>
<p>Hitler now turned his eyes on Great Britain, which stood alone against him. He ordered his generals to draw up plans for an invasion, code named <a href="/wiki/Operation_Sea_Lion" title="Operation Sea Lion">Operation Sea Lion</a>, and ordered the Luftwaffe to launch a massive air war against the British isles, which would come to be known as the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain" title="Battle of Britain">Battle of Britain</a>. The British at first suffered steady losses, but eventually managed to turn the air war against Germany, taking down 2,698 German planes throughout the summer of 1940 to only 915 <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> (RAF) losses.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The key turning point came when the Germans discontinued successful attacks against British airplane factories and radar command and coordination stations and turned to civilian bombing known as <a href="/wiki/Terror_bombing" class="mw-redirect" title="Terror bombing">terror bombing</a> using the distinctive "bomb" sound created by the German dive-bomber, the <a href="/wiki/Stuka" class="mw-redirect" title="Stuka">Stuka</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The switch came after a small British bombing force had attacked Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Hitler was infuriated. However, his decision to switch the attacks' focus allowed the British to rebuild the RAF and eventually force the Germans to indefinitely postpone Sea Lion.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The importance of the Battle of Britain is that it marked the first of Hitler's defeats, however its overall impact was overshadowed by his later blunders in the east. Secondly, it marked the advent of <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">radar</a> as a major weapon in modern air war.  With radar, squadrons of fighters could be quickly assembled to respond to incoming bombers attempting to bomb civilian targets. It also allowed the identification of the type and a guess at the number of incoming enemy aircraft, as well as tracking of friendly airplanes.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Operation_Barbarossa">Operation Barbarossa</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Operation Barbarossa"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Hitler, taken aback by his defeat over the skies of Britain, now turned his gaze eastward to the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. Despite having signed the non-aggression pact with Stalin, Hitler despised communism and wished to destroy it in the land of its birth. He originally planned to launch the attack in early spring of 1941 to avoid the disastrous Russian winter. However, a pro-allied coup in <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> and Mussolini's almost utter defeat in his invasion of Greece from occupied <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> prompted Hitler to launch a personal campaign of revenge in Yugoslavia and to occupy Greece at the same time.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Greeks would have a bitter revenge of sorts; the attack caused a delay of several crucial weeks of the invasion of the USSR, potentially hampering it.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:World_War_II_in_Europe,_1942.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/World_War_II_in_Europe%2C_1942.svg/220px-World_War_II_in_Europe%2C_1942.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="207" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/World_War_II_in_Europe%2C_1942.svg/330px-World_War_II_in_Europe%2C_1942.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/World_War_II_in_Europe%2C_1942.svg/440px-World_War_II_in_Europe%2C_1942.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="519" data-file-height="488"></a><figcaption>Europe at the height of German control in 1942</figcaption></figure>
<p>On 22 June 1941, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">Hitler attacked Stalin with the largest army the world had ever seen</a>. Over three million men and their weapons were put into service against the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Stalin had been warned about the attack, both by other countries and by his own intelligence network, but he had refused to believe it. Therefore, the Soviet army was largely unprepared and suffered massive setbacks in the early part of the war, despite Stalin's orders to counterattack the Germans.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Throughout 1941, German forces, divided into 3 army groups (Army Group A, Army Group B, and Army Group C), occupied the territories of the present day <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, laid siege to <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Leningrad</a> (present day Saint Petersburg), and advanced to within 15 miles of Moscow. At this critical moment, the Soviet people stalled the German <i><a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a></i> to a halt at the gates of Moscow. Stalin had planned to evacuate the city, and had already moved important government functions, but decided to stay and rally the city. Recently arrived troops from the east under the command of Marshal <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Zhukov" title="Georgy Zhukov">Georgy Zhukov</a> counterattacked the Germans and drove them from Moscow.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Mussolini had launched an offensive in North Africa from Italian-controlled <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> into British-controlled Egypt. However, the British smashed the Italians and were on the verge of taking Libya. Hitler decided to help by sending in a few thousand troops, a <i>Luftwaffe</i> division, and the first-rate general <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Rommel" title="Erwin Rommel">Erwin Rommel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Rommel managed to use his small force to repeatedly smash massively superior British forces and to recapture the port city of <a href="/wiki/Tobruk" title="Tobruk">Tobruk</a> and advance into <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>. However, Hitler, embroiled in his invasion of the Soviet Union, refused to send Rommel any more troops, causing Rommel to retreat and preventing him from seizing the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, where Axis-friendly regimes had taken root in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Persia</a> (present-day <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>After the winter, Hitler launched a fresh offensive in the spring of 1942, with the aim of capturing the oil-rich Caucacus and the city of <a href="/wiki/Stalingrad" class="mw-redirect" title="Stalingrad">Stalingrad</a>. However, he repeatedly switched his troops to where they were not needed. The offensive bogged down, and the entire <a href="/wiki/6th_Army_(Wehrmacht)" title="6th Army (Wehrmacht)">6th Army</a>, considered the best of German troops, was trapped in Stalingrad. Hitler now refused to let 6th Army break out. He insisted that the German army would force its way in. Hermann Gring also assured Hitler that the <i>Luftwaffe</i> could supply the 6th Army adequately, when it could in reality only supply a minute fraction of the needed <a href="/wiki/Ammunition" title="Ammunition">ammunition</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ration" class="mw-redirect" title="Ration">rations</a>. Eventually, the starved 6th Army surrendered, dealing a severe blow to the Germans. In the end, the defeat at Stalingrad was the turning point for the war in the east.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Meanwhile, the Japanese had attacked the United States at <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor" title="Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a> in Hawaii on 7 December 1941. This disastrous attack forced the Americans into the war. Parts of the German brass advised against declaring war on the US, arguing that since Japan was the aggressor, the <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Pact" title="Tripartite Pact">Tripartite Pact</a> didn't bind Germany to do so. However, Hitler hoped that Japan would be able to quickly defeat the US and then turn its attention on helping the effort against Russia. Both Germany and Italy declared war on the United States a few days after the attack.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Turning_tides">Turning tides</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Turning tides"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:A_British_soldier_gives_a_V-for-Victory_sign_to_German_prisoners_captured_at_El_Alamein,_26_October_1942._E18522.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/A_British_soldier_gives_a_V-for-Victory_sign_to_German_prisoners_captured_at_El_Alamein%2C_26_October_1942._E18522.jpg/220px-A_British_soldier_gives_a_V-for-Victory_sign_to_German_prisoners_captured_at_El_Alamein%2C_26_October_1942._E18522.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="219" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/A_British_soldier_gives_a_V-for-Victory_sign_to_German_prisoners_captured_at_El_Alamein%2C_26_October_1942._E18522.jpg/330px-A_British_soldier_gives_a_V-for-Victory_sign_to_German_prisoners_captured_at_El_Alamein%2C_26_October_1942._E18522.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/A_British_soldier_gives_a_V-for-Victory_sign_to_German_prisoners_captured_at_El_Alamein%2C_26_October_1942._E18522.jpg/440px-A_British_soldier_gives_a_V-for-Victory_sign_to_German_prisoners_captured_at_El_Alamein%2C_26_October_1942._E18522.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="796"></a><figcaption>A British soldier gives a <a href="/wiki/V_sign" title="V sign">V gesture</a> to German prisoners captured at El Alamein, 26 October 1942</figcaption></figure>
<p>Throughout the rest of 1942 and 1943, the Soviets began to gain ground against the Germans after some victories like the tank battle of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kursk" title="Battle of Kursk">Kursk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> By this time, Rommel had been forced to abandon North Africa after a defeat by <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Montgomery" title="Bernard Montgomery">Montgomery</a> at <a href="/wiki/El_Alamein" title="El Alamein">El Alamein</a> in what was the first decisive victory of the Allies over the Germany army, leading Churchill to declare it "<a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill#&quot;We_shall_never_surrender&quot;" title="Winston Churchill">the end of the beginning</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On several fronts, the <i>Wehrmacht</i> had encountered serious casualties that it could not replace. Hitler also insisted on a "hold at all costs" policy which forbade relinquishing any ground. He followed a "fight to the last man" policy that was completely ineffective. By the beginning of 1944, Hitler had lost all initiative in the Soviet Union, and was struggling even to hold back the tide turning against him.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>From 1942 to 1944, the United States and Britain acted in only a limited manner in the European theater, much to the chagrin of Stalin. They drove out the Germans in Africa, invading <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> on 8 November 1942.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Then, on 10 July 1943, the Allies invaded <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a>, in preparation for an advance through Italy, the "soft underbelly" of the Axis, as <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> called it. On 9 September, the invasion of Italy began.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> By the winter of 1943, the southern half of Italy was in Allied hands. The Italians, most of whom did not really support the war, had already turned against Mussolini. In July, he had been stripped of power and taken prisoner, though the Italians feigned continued support of the Axis. On 8 September, the Italians formally surrendered,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> but most of Italy not in Allied hands was controlled by German troops and those loyal to Mussolini's (Mussolini had been freed by German paratroopers) new <a href="/wiki/Italian_Social_Republic" title="Italian Social Republic">Italian Social Republic</a>, which in reality consisted of the shrinking zone of German control. The Germans offered staunch resistance, but by 4 June 1944, Rome had fallen.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic" title="Battle of the Atlantic">Battle of the Atlantic</a> took place from 1942 to 1944 and was described as "longest, largest, and most complex naval battle in history".<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Germans hoped to sever the vital supply lines between Britain and America, sinking many tons of shipping with <a href="/wiki/U-boats" class="mw-redirect" title="U-boats">U-boats</a>, German submarines. However, the development of the <a href="/wiki/Destroyer" title="Destroyer">destroyer</a> and aircraft with a longer patrol range were effective at countering the U-boat threat and by December 1943, the Germans had lost the battle.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Operation_Overlord">Operation Overlord</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Operation Overlord"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>On 6 June 1944, the Western Allies finally launched the long-awaited assault on "Fortress Europe" so wanted by Stalin. The offensive, codenamed <a href="/wiki/Operation_Overlord" title="Operation Overlord">Operation Overlord</a>, began the early morning hours of 6 June. The day, known as <a href="/wiki/D-day" class="mw-redirect" title="D-day">D-day</a>, was marked by foul weather.  Rommel, who was now in charge of defending France against possible Allied attack, thought the Allies would not attack during the stormy weather, and was on holiday in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Besides this, the Germans were expecting an attack, but at the natural harbor of <a href="/wiki/Calais" title="Calais">Calais</a> and not the beaches of <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a>; They did not know about the Allies' <a href="/wiki/Mulberry_Harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="Mulberry Harbour">artificial harbours</a>, and false leads planted by the Allies suggested Calais as the landing site.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Approaching_Omaha.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Approaching_Omaha.jpg/220px-Approaching_Omaha.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Approaching_Omaha.jpg/330px-Approaching_Omaha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Approaching_Omaha.jpg/440px-Approaching_Omaha.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2147"></a><figcaption>U.S. assault troops approaching <a href="/wiki/Omaha_Beach" title="Omaha Beach">Omaha Beach</a>, 6 June 1944.</figcaption></figure>
<p>By this time, the war was looking ever darker for Germany. On 20 July 1944, a group of conspiring German officers attempted to assassinate Hitler. The bomb they used did injure him, but the second was not used, and a table shielded Hitler in a stroke of luck.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The plotters still could have launched a coup, but only the head of occupied Paris acted, arresting <a href="/wiki/SS" class="mw-redirect" title="SS">SS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gestapo" title="Gestapo">Gestapo</a> forces in the city. The German propaganda minister, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Goebbels" title="Joseph Goebbels">Joseph Goebbels</a>, rallied the Nazis and hunted down the conspirators, arresting up to 7000 people in the wake of the plot, according to some estimates.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In France, the Allies took Normandy and finally Paris on 25 August.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In the east, the Soviets had advanced almost to the former Polish-Soviet border. At this time, Hitler introduced the <a href="/wiki/V-weapons" title="V-weapons">V-weapons</a>, the <a href="/wiki/V-1_flying_bomb" title="V-1 flying bomb">V-1 flying bomb</a> and, later, the <a href="/wiki/V-2" class="mw-redirect" title="V-2">V-2</a>, the first rockets used in modern warfare. The V-1 was often intercepted by air pilots, but the V-2 was extremely fast and carried a large payload. However, this advance came too late in the war to have any real effect.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Germans were also on the verge of introducing a number of terrifying new weapons, including advanced jet aircraft, which were too fast for ordinary propeller aircraft, and submarine improvements which would allow the Germans to again fight effectively in the Atlantic. All this came too late to save Hitler. Although a September invasion of The Netherlands failed, the Allies made steady advances. In the winter of 1944, Hitler put everything into one last desperate gamble in the West, known as the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Bulge" title="Battle of the Bulge">Battle of the Bulge</a>, which, despite an initial advance, was a failure, because the introduction of new Allied tanks and low troop numbers among the Germans prevented any real action being taken. Nevertheless, it was one of the bloodiest battles of the war and <a href="/wiki/List_of_battles_with_most_United_States_military_fatalities" title="List of battles with most United States military fatalities">the second costliest battle in the history of the American Army</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Final_days">Final days</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Final days"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In early February 1945, the three Allied leaders, <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt" class="mw-redirect" title="Franklin Delano Roosevelt">Franklin Roosevelt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>, met at newly liberated <a href="/wiki/Yalta" title="Yalta">Yalta</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Crimean Peninsula">Crimea</a> in the Soviet Union in the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Here, they agreed upon a plan to divide post-war Europe. Most of the east went to Stalin, who agreed to allow free elections in Eastern Europe, which he never did. The west went to Britain, France, and the U.S. Post-war Germany would be split between the four, as would Berlin. This division of spheres of influence would set up international diplomacy for the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> that would dominate the second half of the century.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>At the beginning of 1945, Hitler was on his last strings. The Soviets launched a devastating attack from Poland into Germany and Eastern Europe, intending to take Berlin. The Germans collapsed in the West, allowing the Allies to fan out across Germany. However, the Supreme Allied Commander, American general <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a>, refused to strike for Berlin, and instead became obsessed with reports of possible guerrilla activity in southern Germany, which in reality existed mainly in the propaganda of Joseph Goebbels.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> By 25 April the Soviets had besieged Berlin. Hitler remained in the city in a bunker under the <a href="/wiki/Reich_Chancellery" title="Reich Chancellery">Chancellery</a> garden. On 30 April he committed suicide by shooting himself, after a ritual wedding with his longtime mistress <a href="/wiki/Eva_Braun" title="Eva Braun">Eva Braun</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Germans held out another 7 days under <a href="/wiki/Karl_D%C3%B6nitz" title="Karl Dnitz">Admiral Doenitz</a>, their new leader, but the Germans surrendered unconditionally on 7 May 1945, ending the war in Europe (see <a href="/wiki/V-E_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="V-E Day">V-E Day</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Rivalries that had begun during the war, combined with the sense of strength in the victorious powers, laid the foundations of the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a> and of the Cold War.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="The_war_in_the_Pacific">The war in the Pacific</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: The war in the Pacific"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Asiatic-Pacific_Theater" class="mw-redirect" title="Asiatic-Pacific Theater">Asiatic-Pacific Theater</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading5"><h5 id="Background">Background</h5><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Background"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The first event that is usually linked to the later Pacific conflict was the <a href="/wiki/Mukden_Incident" class="mw-redirect" title="Mukden Incident">Mukden Incident</a> of 18 September 1931, during which the Japanese military staged the bombing of the <a href="/wiki/South_Manchuria_Railway" title="South Manchuria Railway">South Manchuria Railway</a> and pinned the blame on Chinese dissidents.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Japan then used this as <a href="/wiki/Casus_belli" title="Casus belli">pretext</a> to <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Japanese invasion of Manchuria">invade northeastern China</a> the next day and turn the region of <a href="/wiki/Manchuria" title="Manchuria">Manchuria</a> into the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Puppet_state" title="Puppet state">puppet state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Manchukuo" title="Manchukuo">Manchukuo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> After the League of Nations commissioned the 1932 <a href="/wiki/Lytton_Report" title="Lytton Report">Lytton Report</a>, which exposed the Mukden Incident as a Japanese ruse, Japan was left internationally isolated, withdrawing from the League of Nations in March 1933. In 1934 Manchukuo became a constitutional monarchy and the former Chinese Emperor <a href="/wiki/Puyi" title="Puyi">Pu Yi</a> was placed on the throne, despite the real power being held by Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Despite relations between Japan and China suffering because the occupation of Manchuria, the situation did not turn into all-out war until 7 July 1937, when a dispute between Chinese and Japanese soldiers turned into a battle during the <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo_Bridge_Incident" class="mw-redirect" title="Marco Polo Bridge Incident">Marco Polo Bridge Incident</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> This, in turn, led to a further escalation of the hostilities, leading to the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a>, one of the deadliest conflicts in human history.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Japan enjoyed some early major victories, capturing both <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Shanghai" title="Battle of Shanghai">Shanghai</a> and the Chinese capital of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nanjing" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Nanjing">Nanjing</a> in 1937 and forcing the Chinese central government 's relocation to <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chongqing</a>. Following Chinese victories in <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Changsha_(1939)" title="Battle of Changsha (1939)">Changsha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_South_Guangxi" title="Battle of South Guangxi">Guangxi</a> in 1939, the war reached somewhat of a stalemate, with Japan controlling the large cities, but being unable to rule the vast countryside.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On 27 September 1940, Japan became cosignatories of the <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Pact" title="Tripartite Pact">Tripartite Pact</a>, joining a military alliance with Germany and Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Japanese_Expansion">Japanese Expansion</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Japanese Expansion"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:USS_West_Virginia2.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/USS_West_Virginia2.jpg/220px-USS_West_Virginia2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/USS_West_Virginia2.jpg/330px-USS_West_Virginia2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/USS_West_Virginia2.jpg/440px-USS_West_Virginia2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4560" data-file-height="3654"></a><figcaption>USS <i>West Virginia</i> during the attack on Pearl Harbor</figcaption></figure>
<p>On 7 December 1941, Japan launched a surprise attack on the American base at <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor" title="Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a> as a mean of preventing the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Pacific_Fleet" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Pacific Fleet">U.S. Pacific Fleet</a> from interfering with its planned expansion in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The next day, following Roosevelt's <a href="/wiki/Infamy_Speech" class="mw-redirect" title="Infamy Speech">Infamy Speech</a>, the United States declared war on Japan, marking the official entry of both nations in World War 2.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> At the same time, Japan also launched attacks on <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, the British colonies of <a href="/wiki/British_Malaya" title="British Malaya">Malaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> and American military bases in <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wake_Island" title="Wake Island">Wake Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">the Philippines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The next six months were dominated by Japanese victories against the Allied forces, already war-weary and stretched thin after two years of war in Europe and North Africa. Japan managed to capture <a href="/wiki/British_Burma" class="mw-redirect" title="British Burma">British Burma</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bali" title="Bali">Bali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timor" title="Timor">Timor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In March 1942, days before the surrender of the Philippines, general Douglas MacArthur, who came out of retirement to become commander of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Forces_in_the_Far_East" title="United States Army Forces in the Far East">United States Army Forces in the Far East</a> at the onset of the war, <a href="/wiki/Douglas_MacArthur%27s_escape_from_the_Philippines" title="Douglas MacArthur's escape from the Philippines">was forced to flee and narrowly escape</a> to Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On 19 February 1942, Japan also launched a devastating aerial attack on the Australian city of Darwin, in what was the first attack by a foreign power on Australian soil.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The turning of the tide came in early May, during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Coral_Sea" title="Battle of the Coral Sea">Battle of the Coral Sea</a>, which proved the first strategic victory of the Allies against Japanese expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> This was followed one month later by the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Midway" title="Battle of Midway">Battle of Midway</a>, in which the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">US Navy</a> defeated an attacking Japanese fleet, inflicting devastating damage on the attacking force. The Battle of Midway is widely considered the most important naval battle of the Pacific Campaign and has even been described as "the most stunning and decisive blow in the history of naval warfare"<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The reasons usually given for the resounding victory are Japanese overconfidence in their own forces, poor planning and the intercepting of Japanese battle plans by the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The losses suffered during this Battle of Midway, paired with the campaign of attrition that was taking place in <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands_campaign" title="Solomon Islands campaign">Solomon Islands</a>, left Japan unable to replenish its forces and turned the tides of war against it. By August 1942, the Allied forces were on the offensive, earning victories in the <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea_campaign" title="New Guinea campaign">New Guinea campaign</a> at <a href="/wiki/Guadalcanal_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Guadalcanal Campaign">Guadalcanal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Milne_Bay" title="Battle of Milne Bay">Milne Bay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Buna%E2%80%93Gona" title="Battle of BunaGona">Buna-Gona</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Allied_offensive">Allied offensive</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Allied offensive"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
