Other companies, starting with <a href="/wiki/Compaq" title="Compaq">Compaq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reverse_engineered" class="mw-redirect" title="Reverse engineered">reverse engineered</a> the BIOS and released <a href="/wiki/PC_compatible" class="mw-redirect" title="PC compatible">PC compatible</a> computers that soon became the dominant architecture.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>242<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>243<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, which produced an operating system for the PC, rode this wave of popularity to become the world's leading software company.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>244<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The 1980s heralded the <a href="/wiki/Information_Age" title="Information Age">Information Age</a>. The rise of computer applications and <a href="/wiki/Data_processing" title="Data processing">data processing</a> made ethereal "information" as valuable as physical commodities. This brought about new concerns surrounding intellectual property issues. The U.S. Government made algorithms patentable, forming the basis of <a href="/wiki/Software_patent" title="Software patent">software patents</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>245<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The controversy over these and <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_software" title="Proprietary software">proprietary software</a> led <a href="/wiki/Richard_Stallman" title="Richard Stallman">Richard Stallman</a> to create the <a href="/wiki/Free_Software_Foundation" title="Free Software Foundation">Free Software Foundation</a> and begin the <a href="/wiki/GNU" title="GNU">GNU Project</a>, paving the way for a <a href="/wiki/Free_software_movement" title="Free software movement">free software movement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>246<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Computers also became a usable platform for entertainment. Computer games were first developed by software programmers exercising their creativity on large systems at universities, but these efforts became commercially successful in <a href="/wiki/Arcade_game" title="Arcade game">arcade games</a> such as <i><a href="/wiki/Pong" title="Pong">Pong</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Space_Invaders" title="Space Invaders">Space Invaders</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>247<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Once the home computer market was established, young programmers in their bedrooms became the core of a youthful <a href="/wiki/Video_game_industry" title="Video game industry">video game industry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>248<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In order to take advantage of advancing technology, <a href="/wiki/Games_console" class="mw-redirect" title="Games console">games consoles</a> were created. Like arcade systems, these machines had custom hardware designed to do game-oriented operations (such as <a href="/wiki/Sprite_(computer_science)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sprite (computer science)">sprites</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parallax_scrolling" title="Parallax scrolling">parallax scrolling</a>) in preference to general purpose computing tasks.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>249<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:IBM_PC_5150.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/IBM_PC_5150.jpg/250px-IBM_PC_5150.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="184" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/IBM_PC_5150.jpg/375px-IBM_PC_5150.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/IBM_PC_5150.jpg/500px-IBM_PC_5150.jpg 2x" data-file-width="962" data-file-height="708"></a><figcaption>The first model of the <a href="/wiki/IBM_PC" class="mw-redirect" title="IBM PC">IBM PC</a>, the personal computer whose successors would fill the world.</figcaption></figure><p><a href="/wiki/Computer_network" title="Computer network">Computer networks</a> appeared in two main styles; the <a href="/wiki/Local_area_network" title="Local area network">local area network</a>, linking computers in an office or school to each other, and the <a href="/wiki/Wide_area_network" title="Wide area network">wide area network</a>, linking the local area networks together. Initially, computers depended on the <a href="/wiki/PSTN" class="mw-redirect" title="PSTN">telephone networks</a> to link to each other, spawning the <a href="/wiki/Bulletin_board_system" title="Bulletin board system">Bulletin Board</a> sub-culture.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>250<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> However, a <a href="/wiki/DARPA" title="DARPA">DARPA</a> project to create bomb-proof computer networks led to the creation of the Internet, a network of networks. The core of this network was the robust <a href="/wiki/TCP/IP" class="mw-redirect" title="TCP/IP">TCP/IP</a> <a href="/wiki/Network_protocol" class="mw-redirect" title="Network protocol">network protocol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>251<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Thanks to efforts from <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>, the Internet grew beyond its military role when universities and commercial businesses were permitted to connect their networks to it.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>252<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>253<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The main impetus for this was <a href="/wiki/Electronic_mail" class="mw-redirect" title="Electronic mail">electronic mail</a>, a far faster and convenient form of communication than a conventional letter and memo distribution, and the <a href="/wiki/File_Transfer_Protocol" title="File Transfer Protocol">File Transfer Protocol</a> (FTP). However, the Internet remained largely unknown to the general public, who were used to Bulletin Boards and services like <a href="/wiki/Compuserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Compuserve">Compuserve</a> and <a href="/wiki/AOL" title="AOL">America Online</a>. This changed when <a href="/wiki/Tim_Berners-Lee" title="Tim Berners-Lee">Tim Berners-Lee</a> devised a simpler form of <a href="/wiki/Vannevar_Bush" title="Vannevar Bush">Vannevar Bush</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Hypertext" title="Hypertext">hypertext</a>, which he dubbed the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>254<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> "The Web" suddenly changed the Internet into a printing press beyond the geographic boundaries of physical countries; it was termed "<a href="/wiki/Cyberspace" title="Cyberspace">cyberspace</a>". Anyone with a computer and an Internet connection could write pages in the simple <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a> format and publish their thoughts to the world.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>255<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Web's immense success also fueled the commercial use of the Internet. Convenient home shopping had been an element of "visions of the future" since the development of the telephone, but now the race was on to provide convenient, interactive consumerism.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>256<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Companies trading through websites became known as "<a href="/wiki/Dot_com_company" class="mw-redirect" title="Dot com company">dot coms</a>", due to the ".com" suffix of commercial Internet addresses.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>257<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The change of the century also lead to the fear and paranoia of <a href="/wiki/Year_2000_problem" title="Year 2000 problem">Y2K</a>, where it was hypothesized that the World's computers would glitch and cause havoc on banks, prisons, transit systems and more.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="The_world_at_the_end_of_the_century">The world at the end of the century</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Key_events_of_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: The world at the end of the century"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1990s" title="1990s">1990s</a></div>
<p>By the end of the century, more technological advances and scientific discoveries had been made than in all of preceding history. Communications and information technology, transportation technology, and medical advances have radically altered daily lives. Europe appeared to be at a sustainable peace for the first time in recorded history. The people of the Indian subcontinent, a sixth of the world population at the end of the century, had attained indigenous independence for the first time in centuries. China, an ancient nation comprising a fifth of the world's population, was finally open to the world in a new and powerful synthesis of West and East, creating a new state after the near-complete destruction of the old cultural order.  With the end of colonialism and the Cold War, nearly a billion people in Africa were left with truly independent new nation-states, some cut from whole cloth, standing up after centuries of foreign domination.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>258<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Global_Warming_Predictions_Map.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Global_Warming_Predictions_Map.jpg/280px-Global_Warming_Predictions_Map.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="204" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Global_Warming_Predictions_Map.jpg/420px-Global_Warming_Predictions_Map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ad/Global_Warming_Predictions_Map.jpg 2x" data-file-width="559" data-file-height="408"></a><figcaption>The geographic distribution of surface warming during the 21st century calculated by the <a href="/wiki/HadCM3" title="HadCM3">HadCM3</a> climate model if a business as usual scenario is assumed for economic growth and greenhouse gas emissions. In this figure, the globally averaged warming corresponds to 3.0&nbsp;C (5.4&nbsp;F).</figcaption></figure>
<p>The world was undergoing its second major period of <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a>; <a href="/wiki/First_globalization" title="First globalization">the first</a>, which started in the 19th century, having been terminated by World War I.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>259<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Since the US was in a position of almost unchallenged domination, a major part of the process was <a href="/wiki/Americanization" title="Americanization">Americanization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>260<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> This led to anti-Western and <a href="/wiki/Anti-Americanism" title="Anti-Americanism">anti-American</a> feelings in parts of the world, especially the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>261<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The influence of China and India was also rising, as the world's largest populations, long marginalized by the West and by their rulers, were rapidly integrating with the world economy.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>262<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>However, several problems face the world. The gap between rich and poor nations continued to widen. Some said that this problem could not be fixed, that there was a set amount of wealth and it could only be shared by so many. Others said that the powerful nations with large economies were not doing enough to help improve the rapidly evolving economies of the <a href="/wiki/Third_World" title="Third World">Third World</a>. However, developing countries faced many challenges, including the scale of the task to be surmounted, rapidly growing populations, and the need to protect the environment and the cost that goes along with it.
</p><p>Terrorism, dictatorship, and the spread of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear weapons">nuclear weapons</a> were other issues requiring attention. The world was still blighted by small-scale wars and other violent conflicts, fueled by competition over resources and ethnic conflicts. <a href="/wiki/Despotism" title="Despotism">Despots</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Kim_Jong-il" class="mw-redirect" title="Kim Jong-il">Kim Jong-il</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> continued to lead their nations toward the development of nuclear weapons.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>263<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Disease threatened to destabilize many regions of the world. New viruses such as <a href="/wiki/SARS" title="SARS">SARS</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Nile_virus" title="West Nile virus">West Nile</a> continued to spread.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>264<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>265<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In poor nations, <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> and other diseases affected the majority of the population. Millions were infected with HIV, the virus which causes AIDS. The virus was becoming an <a href="/wiki/AIDS_in_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="AIDS in Africa">epidemic in southern Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>266<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Perhaps most importantly, it was speculated that in the long term, environmental problems threatened the planet's livability. The most serious problem was <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" class="mw-redirect" title="Global warming">global warming</a>, which was predicted to frequently flood coastal areas, due to human-caused emission of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a>, particularly <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> produced by the burning of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>. Like the threat of a <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_warfare" title="Nuclear warfare">nuclear world war</a>, the shift of <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> has since <a href="/wiki/Damocles" title="Damocles">added to the fear</a> of the possibility of <a href="/wiki/Human_extinction" title="Human extinction">human extinction</a>, although not overnight but over several decades.<sup id="cite_ref-Rich_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rich-267"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>267<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> This prompted many nations to negotiate and sign the <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto treaty</a>, which set mandatory limits on carbon dioxide emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>268<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Millennium_celebrations" title="Millennium celebrations">celebration of the 20th centurys ending</a> expressed the popular opinion that <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve" title="New Year's Eve">New Year's Eve</a> 1999 and <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day" title="New Year's Day">New Year's Day</a> 2000 marked the <a href="/wiki/Millennium#Debate_over_millennium_celebrations" title="Millennium">turn of the millennium</a>, while strictly speaking the 20th century ended on New Year's Eve 2000 and the 21st century began on New Year's Day 2001.
</p>
